// Place them right before module.exports at the bottom

// ── 4 EXPLANATION STYLES ──────────────────────────────────────────────────

function build4Styles(result, f_list) {

return {

data: buildDataStyle(result, f_list),

story: buildStoryStyle(result, f_list),

compare: buildCompareStyle(result, f_list),

action: buildActionStyle(result, f_list)

};

}

function buildDataStyle(result, f_list) {

// Same as current fallback

if (result.tie.length \> 1) {

return \`\${result.tie.join(\" and \")} are equally optimal. Both scored identically.\`;

}

const winner = result.winner;

const winnerBreakdown = result.detailed_breakdown\[winner\];

let bestFeature = f_list\[0\];

let lowestPenalty = Infinity;

for (let f of f_list) {

if (winnerBreakdown\[f\].weighted_penalty \< lowestPenalty) {

lowestPenalty = winnerBreakdown\[f\].weighted_penalty;

bestFeature = f;

}

}

const winnerScore = result.agg_sum\[winner\].toFixed(2);

return \`Based on your priorities, the system recommends \${winner} (\${winnerScore} points). \${lowestPenalty === 0 ? \`Perfect match on \${bestFeature}.\` : \`Strongest on \${bestFeature}.\`}\`;

}

function buildStoryStyle(result, f_list) {

if (result.tie.length \> 1) {

return \`It\'s a tie between \${result.tie.join(\" and \")}. Both are equally strong choices.\`;

}

const winner = result.winner;

const second = result.ranking\[1\]?.product;

return \`\${winner} emerges as the strongest choice. While \${second \|\| \"other options\"} had advantages in specific areas, \${winner} strikes the best overall balance for what you\'re looking for.\`;

}

function buildCompareStyle(result, f_list) {

if (result.tie.length \> 1) {

return \`\${result.tie.join(\" and \")} scored identically. No meaningful difference.\`;

}

const top3 = result.ranking.slice(0, 3);

let text = \"Why the ranking:\\n\";

top3.forEach(({ product, score }) =\> {

const breakdown = result.detailed_breakdown\[product\];

const best = f_list.reduce((a, b) =\>

breakdown\[a\].weighted_penalty \< breakdown\[b\].weighted_penalty ? a : b

);

text += \`• \${product}: Best at \${best}, score \${score.toFixed(2)}\\n\`;

});

return text;

}

function buildActionStyle(result, f_list) {

if (result.tie.length \> 1) {

return \`Choose either \${result.tie.join(\" or \")}. Identical value.\`;

}

const winner = result.winner;

const score = result.agg_sum\[winner\].toFixed(2);

const breakdown = result.detailed_breakdown\[winner\];

let pros = \[\];

let cons = \[\];

f_list.forEach(f =\> {

if (breakdown\[f\].penalty === 0) {

pros.push(f);

} else if (breakdown\[f\].weighted_penalty \> 5) {

cons.push(f);

}

});

let text = \`✓ Choose \${winner} (\${score} pts)\\n\`;

if (pros.length) text += \`Strengths: \${pros.join(\", \")}\\n\`;

if (cons.length) text += \`Trade-off: \${cons.join(\", \")}\`;

return text;

}

// REPLACE your existing module.exports with this:

module.exports = { calculateDecision, generateExplanation, build4Styles };

// In server.js, REPLACE the /api/calculate endpoint with this:

const { calculateDecision, generateExplanation, build4Styles } = require(\"./decisionLogic\");

app.post(\"/api/calculate\", async (req, res) =\> {

try {

const { products_data, features, weights_raw, ideals, directions } = req.body;

const result = calculateDecision(products_data, features, weights_raw, ideals, directions);

// Generate AI explanation (or fallback)

const { explanation, source } = await generateExplanation(result, features);

// Generate all 4 template styles

const styles = build4Styles(result, features);

res.json({

\...result,

explanation,

explanation_source: source,

explanation_styles: styles // NEW: All 4 styles

});

} catch (error) {

console.error(\"Calculation error:\", error.message);

res.status(500).json({ error: error.message });

}

});

// In script.js, ADD these at the top (global state)

let currentStyleIndex = 0;

let allStyles = null;

const styleNames = \[\'data\', \'story\', \'compare\', \'action\'\];

const styleLabels = \[\'📊 Data-Driven\', \'📖 Storytelling\', \'⚖️ Comparative\', \'⚡ Actionable\'\];

// REPLACE your displayResults function\'s explanation section with this:

function displayResults(result) {

const container = document.getElementById(\'results-container\');

// Store styles for refresh button

allStyles = result.explanation_styles;

currentStyleIndex = 0;

let html = \'\';

// Winner/Tie (same as before)

if (result.tie.length === 1) {

html += \`

\<div class=\"winner-card\"\>

\<h3\>🏆 Recommended Choice\</h3\>

\<div style=\"font-size: 2.5rem; margin: 16px 0;\"\>\${result.winner}\</div\>

\<div\>Score: \${result.agg_sum\[result.winner\].toFixed(2)} points\</div\>

\</div\>

\`;

} else {

html += \`

\<div class=\"tie-alert\"\>

\<h3\>🤝 Tie Detected\</h3\>

\<p\>The following options are equally optimal:\</p\>

\<ul\>\${result.tie.map(p =\> \`\<li\>\${p}\</li\>\`).join(\'\')}\</ul\>

\</div\>

\`;

}

// EXPLANATION CARD with REFRESH button

html += \`

\<div class=\"explanation-card\"\>

\<div style=\"display: flex; justify-content: space-between; align-items: center;\"\>

\<h3\>💡 Why This Result?\</h3\>

\<button onclick=\"cycleExplanation()\" class=\"refresh-btn\"\>

🔄 \<span id=\"style-label\"\>\${styleLabels\[0\]}\</span\>

\</button\>

\</div\>

\<p id=\"explanation-text\"\>\${result.explanation}\</p\>

\<span class=\"source-tag\"\>\${result.explanation_source === \'groq\' ? \'⚡ Groq\' : result.explanation_source === \'gemini\' ? \'🤖 Gemini\' : \'📋 Template\'}\</span\>

\</div\>

\`;

// Ranking (same as before)

html += \`\<h3\>📊 Complete Ranking\</h3\>\...\`;

container.innerHTML = html;

}

// ADD this new function

function cycleExplanation() {

if (!allStyles) return;

currentStyleIndex = (currentStyleIndex + 1) % 4;

const styleName = styleNames\[currentStyleIndex\];

document.getElementById(\'explanation-text\').textContent = allStyles\[styleName\];

document.getElementById(\'style-label\').textContent = styleLabels\[currentStyleIndex\];

}

**Core Algorithm (100% Our Logic, No AI)**

-   **File:** backend/decisionLogic.js

-   **Method:** Weighted penalty scoring with distance-from-ideal-point

-   **Features Implemented:**

    -   Normalization (all values → 0-100 scale for fair comparison)

    -   Direction-aware penalties (higher-is-better vs lower-is-better)

    -   Weighted aggregation (user importance ratings → normalized weights)

    -   Tie detection with float tolerance (ε \< 0.001)

    -   Ranking output (sorted by total penalty score)

-   **Stack:** Node.js + Express backend, vanilla HTML/CSS/JS frontend

-   **Port:** localhost:3000

-   **Flow:** 5-step wizard

    1.  Setup (number of products/features)

    2.  Define criteria (name, importance 1-5, direction)

    3.  Enter product values

    4.  Enter ideal values

    5.  View results with ranking + explanations

-   **Primary:** Groq API (Llama 3.3-70B) - Fast, free tier

-   **Backup:** Gemini API (gemini-2.5-flash) - If Groq fails

-   **Final Fallback:** Template-based (offline, always works)

-   **Feature:** 4 explanation styles (Data-Driven, Storytelling, Comparative, Actionable) with refresh button to cycle through

-   **Quality Gate:** Rejects short AI responses (\<50 words), falls back to detailed template

**🐛 Critical Bugs Fixed During Development**

**Bug 1: Normalization Scale Mismatch (Feb 16, Morning)**

-   **Issue:** Comparing normalized product values (0-100) to raw ideal values

-   **Impact:** Completely wrong results

-   **Fix:** Normalize ideal values using same min/max formula

-   **Location:** decisionLogic.js lines 37-45

**Bug 2: Double Penalty Calculation (Feb 16, Afternoon)**

-   **Issue:** d\[i\]\[y\] = abs(actual - ideal) + penalty → counted penalty twice

-   **Impact:** All scores 2x too high

-   **Fix:** Changed to d\[i\]\[y\] = penalty only

-   **Location:** decisionLogic.js lines 58-67

**Bug 3: API Confusion - Grok vs Groq (Feb 17)**

-   **Issue:** Calling api.x.ai (xAI\'s Grok) instead of api.groq.com (Groq/Llama)

-   **Impact:** 400/403 errors on all API calls

-   **Fix:** Learned correct patterns from Antigravity project server.js

    -   Groq: api.groq.com, model llama-3.3-70b-versatile

    -   Gemini: Key in URL (?key=), model gemini-2.5-flash

**Bug 4: One-Line Explanation Collapse (Feb 18)**

-   **Issue:** Multi-line explanations rendering as single compressed line

-   **Impact:** Comparative/Action styles unreadable

-   **Fix:** Added white-space: pre-line; to .explanation-card p in CSS

-   **Additional Fix:** Quality gate to reject short AI responses

\## 🧮 Algorithm Details (For Documentation)

\### Input

\- \`n\` products (n ≥ 2 recommended)

\- \`f\` features (f ≥ 1)

\- Importance ratings per feature (1-5 scale, auto-normalized to sum = 1.0)

\- Direction per feature (True = higher better, False = lower better)

\- Ideal values per feature

\### Process

\`\`\`

1\. Compute min/max per feature across all products

2\. Normalize all product values: (value - min)/(max - min) × 100

3\. Normalize ideal values using same min/max

4\. Calculate penalties:

\- If higher-is-better: penalty = max(0, ideal - actual)

\- If lower-is-better: penalty = max(0, actual - ideal)

5\. Aggregate: total_penalty = Σ(penalty\[i\] × weight\[i\])

6\. Rank by total penalty (ascending)

7\. Detect ties with ε-tolerance (\|score1 - score2\| \< 0.001)

**Output**

-   Winner (or list of tied products)

-   Complete ranking with scores

-   Per-product, per-feature penalty breakdown

-   AI-generated explanation (or template fallback)

-   4 alternative explanation styles

\## ⚠️ Known Limitations (To Document)

\### Current Limitations

1\. \*\*Requires numeric values\*\* - No support for qualitative criteria (e.g., \"good\", \"average\", \"poor\")

2\. \*\*Linear penalty model\*\* - No diminishing returns (gap from 0→10 same as 90→100)

3\. \*\*Singular ideal values\*\* - No range-based criteria support

4\. \*\*No data persistence\*\* - Session-based only, no database

5\. \*\*String comparison\*\* - \"True\"/\"False\" direction is case-sensitive in backend (handled by dropdown in UI)

\### Edge Cases Handled

\- Division by zero when all products identical on a feature → Set normalized value to 50.0

\- Ideal value outside product range → Normalization handles gracefully

\- Float comparison for ties → Epsilon tolerance (\< 0.001)

\- Weights sum validation → Auto-normalize if don\'t sum to 1.0

\-\--

\## 💬 Questions That Might Come Up

\*\*Q: Why not use established MCDM methods like TOPSIS or AHP?\*\*

A: Explainability. Weighted penalty scoring is intuitive for users and transparent in showing how decisions are made. Complex methods would be black boxes.

\*\*Q: Why allow AI in explanation generation if assignment says \"not AI dependent\"?\*\*

A: Core decision logic (normalization, penalties, ranking) is 100% deterministic code. AI only converts our calculated numbers into natural language. Assignment allows AI if role is clearly justified.

\*\*Q: What if APIs are down during evaluation?\*\*

A: System has triple fallback (Groq → Gemini → Template). Template fallback works offline with zero dependencies. Evaluators will always get results.

\*\*Q: How do you handle subjective criteria?\*\*

A: Current version requires numeric values. User must convert subjective judgments to numbers (e.g., \"cultural fit\" → rate 1-10). Future enhancement could add categorical support.

\*\*Q: Why Node.js if you already wrote the algorithm in Python?\*\*

A: Prepares for Phase 2 (web scraping has better libraries in Node.js). Also demonstrates ability to convert logic across languages while maintaining correctness.

# Response 25 : Phase 1.5

You\'ve touched on the \"Core Ambiguity\" of system design. To answer your question: **Phase 1 is mathematically complete, but semantically limited.**

Currently, your system is a \"Logic Engine\" that needs a \"Translation Layer\" to handle the real world. Here are some natural language hints (Phase 1.5 concepts) on how we could bridge that gap without changing the core penalty-scoring logic:

**1. The \"Scale Mapping\" Strategy (The Low-Code Bridge)**

Instead of a free-text input, we could provide a **Likert Scale** in the UI.

-   *User sees:* \"Communication: \[Excellent, Good, Average, Poor\]\"

-   *System processes:* {Excellent: 10, Good: 7, Average: 5, Poor: 2}

-   **Why this works:** It converts subjective judgment into an objective number *before* the math engine even sees it. It satisfies the \"Numerical Input\" requirement of Phase 1 while feeling subjective to the user.

**2. The \"Categorical Distance\" Strategy (The \"Weather\" Example)**

For things like \"Sunny\" vs \"Windy\", we can\'t use 0-100 logic easily.

-   **Hint:** We treat the values as a set. If the Ideal is \"Sunny\", and the product is \"Sunny\", penalty = 0. If it is \"Partly Cloudy\", penalty = 20. If it is \"Windy\", penalty = 50.

-   This requires a \"Distance Matrix\" where we define how far apart different qualitative categories are.

**3. The \"AI Sentiment Pre-Processor\" (The Phase 3 Preview)**

This is where the AI truly justifies its role.

-   **Concept:** The user inputs a review paragraph: *\"The communication was okay but they lacked technical depth.\"*

-   **AI\'s Role:** It \"reads\" the text and outputs a JSON object: 

{Technical: 4, Communication: 6}

.

-   The AI acts as a **feature extractor** that feeds your deterministic penalty engine. This ensures the *decision* is still based on your 100% logic, but the *data entry* is human-friendly.

**Is Phase 1 Complete?**

For the purpose of your assignment\'s Phase 1, yes---the engine works. But for a \"Decision Companion\" to be truly useful, it needs one of these bridges.

**Does one of these approaches (Mapping, Distance Sets, or AI Pre-processing) resonate with you for Phase 1.5/Phase 2?** I\'ve updated the implementation plan to include a research task for this.

# Response 26 : Subjective Feedback Handling

Based on **Vonnue\'s Prompt No. 1** conditions and your Phase 1 logic, here is the breakdown of how to balance manual implementation vs. AI for Phase 1.5.

Vonnue\'s critical rule is: **\"The system should not be a static hard-coded comparison\... but your logic should be explainable (not a black box).\"**

**My Recommendation (The \"Hints\")**

To wow the evaluators, don\'t let the AI \"decide\" the score. Use the AI to **extract** the score from human language, while you handle the **logic**.

1.  **The Manual \"Skeleton\" (Recommended for you to build):** Implement a 

SubjectiveConverter

 function. This function checks if an input is in your manual 

EnumMapping

. If it is (e.g., the user selected \"Good\" from a dropdown), it uses your hard-coded value. This makes your system **work offline** (no AI needed).

2.  **The AI \"Translator\" (Justified Role):** If the user types a free-form review like *\"The weather was a bit chilly but mostly clear,\"* your 

SubjectiveConverter

 won\'t find that in its table. **This is where you call the AI.**

-   **Prompt Hint:** \"Given the travel goal is \'Tropical Paradise\', score the sentiment of this review from 1-10 regarding \'Weather\'.\"

-   **Justification:** \"AI is used strictly as a Natural Language Interpreter to convert qualitative human feedback into numerical data for our deterministic scoring engine.\"

**Why this follows Vonnue\'s conditions:**

-   **Transparent:** You can show exactly how \"Good\" becomes 7.

-   **Not AI-Dependent:** The system still functions perfectly if the API is down (using the manual Enums/Dropdowns).

-   **Explainable:** The final ranking isn\'t a \"Because ChatGPT said so\" result; it\'s \"Because the input was interpreted as 7, which created a penalty of 3 based on our weighted logic.\"

**Verdict:** For Phase 1.5, **Manually implement the Enum and Categorical Mapping.** Use AI only as a \"fail-safe\" or \"interpreter\" for free-text inputs that don\'t match your manual categories.

**Next Step Hint:** Look into how you would structure a 

mapping.js

 file that your 

decisionLogic.js can call before starting the normalization. Do you want to see a conceptual structure of that mapping logic? (No code, just the structure).

# Antigravity Prompt 27 : Distance Matrix Concept

Categorical Proximity 100% Manual. You build a \"Distance Matrix.\" If Ideal: Sunny and Actual: Windy, distance = 8. 0%. This is a structured lookup table. High. Shows \"Design Maturity.\" elaborate on this how do you manually implement this.. CRTICAL DONT GIVE ME EXACT CODE RATHER TEACH ME

# Response 27 : New Concept Explained

To manually implement **Categorical Proximity**, you are essentially building a **\"Mathematical Map of Similarity.\"**

In your Phase 1 code, 

Penalty = \|Ideal - Actual\|

. With categories like \"Sunny\" vs \"Windy\", the computer doesn\'t know the \"distance\" between words. You have to define that distance manually.

Here is the conceptual breakdown of how to build this \"Logic Bridge\" without using AI:

**1. The \"Distance Matrix\" Concept**

Imagine a spreadsheet where every possible category is both a Row and a Column. The value in each cell represents the \"Penalty\" for that specific combination.

-   **Logic:** If the user wants \"Sunny\" (Ideal) and the destination is \"Rainy\" (Actual), your code looks up the intersection and finds an **8 penalty**.

-   **Design Maturity:** This proves you've thought about the *relationship* between choices (e.g., \"Cloudy\" is closer to \"Sunny\" than \"Rainy\" is).

**2. The Implementation Logic (The \"How-To\")**

Instead of a simple subtraction, your 

decisionLogic.js would follow these steps:

1.  **Storage:** Store these tables as nested \"Objects\" (Key-Value pairs). One object per feature (e.g., 

weatherDistances

, 

colorDistances

).

2.  **The Fetcher:** Create a function that takes 

(FeatureName, ValueA, ValueB).

3.  **The Step-Down:**

    -   If 

ValueA == ValueB

, distance is **0**.

-   Look into your 

DistanceMatrix

 for 

ValueA

.

-   Inside that, look for 

ValueB

.

-   If found, that is your **Penalty**.

-   If NOT found (user typed something weird), assign a **Default Max Penalty** (e.g., 10).

**3. The \"Ideal\" Problem**

In Phase 1, you allow users to type raw numbers for Ideals. For Categorical Proximity, you must limit the Ideal to a **Dropdown Choice**.

-   If the feature type is \"Categorical,\" the UI should force the user to pick from your pre-defined map keys (Sunny, Cloudy, etc.).

**Why this is \"High Design Maturity\":**

When you explain this to Vonnue, you can say:

*\"I rejected the idea of letting the AI guess if \'Windy\' is better than \'Rainy\'. Instead, I built a deterministic Proximity Matrix. This ensures that the system\'s decision-making process is 100% transparent and consistent, while still allowing for qualitative criteria that simple math cannot handle.\"*

**The \"Pro Tip\" for your BUILD_PROCESS:**

Mention that you use **Symmetry**. In a good distance matrix, the distance from *Sunny to Rainy* should be the same as *Rainy to Sunny*. If they aren\'t, it\'s an \"Asymmetric Matrix\"---which is even more advanced!

**Does this \"Lookup Table\" logic make sense for how you\'d replace the **

Math.abs()

** subtraction for words?**

# Response 28 : Cleaned Prompt

Here is a **prompt** designed specifically for your AI assistant (like me, Codex, or Claude) to implement **Phase 1.5** into your 

decision-companion

 project.

**Prompt for Phase 1.5: The Hybrid Decision Engine**

**Objective:** Upgrade the existing Decision Companion System to handle **subjective/qualitative criteria** alongside numeric ones. Implement a triple-input strategy: Numeric, Scale-Mapping, and AI Interpretation.

**1. Requirement: Data Structure Update**

Modify the data flow to include a 

featureType

 for each criterion.

-   **Type 1 (Numeric):** Standard raw number input (Phase 1 legacy).

-   **Type 2 (Scale):** Dropdown mapping: *Excellent (10), Very Good (9), Good (8), Above Average (7), Average (6), Below Average (5), Poor (4).*

-   **Type 3 (Review):** Free-form text interpreted by AI into a 1-10 score.

**2. Frontend Changes (**

index.html** & **

script.js**)**

-   **Step 2 (Criteria):** Add a dropdown next to each Criterion Name to select its **Type** (Numeric, Scale, or Review).

-   **Step 3 (Product Data):** Dynamically render the input fields based on the selected Type:

    -   If Numeric: 

\<input type=\"number\"\>

-   If Scale: 

\<select\>

 with the 7 human-friendly options.

-   If Review: 

\<textarea placeholder=\"Enter text description\...\"\>

-   **Step 4 (Ideals):** Similarly, if a feature is \"Scale\", the Ideal input should be the same dropdown. If \"Review,\" the Ideal should be a target description or a target score (1-10).

**3. Backend Changes (**

server.js** & **

decisionLogic.js**)**

Update 

calculateDecision to perform **Preprocessing** before the normalization loop:

-   **Enum Mapper:** Create an object mapping the Scale string values (e.g., \"Excellent\") to their numeric equivalents.

-   **AI Score Extractor:**

    -   Create a function 

extractScoreFromText(text, featureName, idealDescription)

.

-   Content: Call the Groq/Gemini API with a system prompt: *\"You are a feature extractor. Analyze the following review for the feature \'\${featureName}\'. Based on the target \'\${idealDescription}\', output ONLY a single integer from 1 to 10 where 10 is a perfect match.\"*

```{=html}
<!-- -->
```
-   **The Fallback Loop:**

    -   Wrap the AI Score Extractor in a try-catch.

    -   **CRITICAL:** If the AI fails (Server Busy/403/Empty), the system must respond with a specific error code that triggers the frontend to ask the user: *\"AI interpretation failed. Would you like to manually categorize this as (scale options)?\"*

**4. Logic Integration**

-   Ensure the converted scores (from Scale or Review) are injected into the 

products_data

 object exactly like original numbers so the existing logic (Normalization -\> Penalty -\> Ranking) remains 100% deterministic and \"mine.\"

**5. UI/UX Polishing**

# Response 29 : Design Solutions to 6 Problems

Great questions --- all 6 are design decisions, not just coding questions. Let me walk through each one using your **Juice example** specifically.

**Doubt 1: Must the Ideal Input Type Match the Feature Type?**

**Yes, ideally (pun intended).** Here is why:

-   Feature: **Price (Numeric)** → Ideal should also be a **number** (e.g., 

₹50

).

-   Feature: **Quality (Scale)** → Ideal should be a **Scale grade** (e.g., 

Excellent

).

-   Feature: **Expert Opinion (Review)** → Ideal should be a **short description**, NOT a review paragraph.

For \"Expert Opinion,\" the ideal could be a short target phrase that *the user provides once*, like:

*\"I want a juice that is healthy and tasty.\"*

This is your **reference point.** Every product\'s review is then scored against this one short ideal description. The user doesn\'t write 4 separate ideals --- just one target intention.

**Key Rule:** 

\"I hope its a price that doesn\'t sadden my heart\"

 is not a valid numeric ideal. The UI should enforce type-matching --- if the feature is Numeric, the ideal input box should be 

type=\"number\"

 only.

**Doubt 2: When Does the AI Process the Reviews, and Can There Be a Loading Screen?**

**Yes, loading is necessary and there\'s a natural pause point.**

The timeline is:

User fills Step 3 (reviews for 4 products)

↓

User fills Step 4 (ideal: \"Healthy, Tasty juice\")

↓

User clicks \"Calculate Decision 🚀\"

↓

Backend receives everything → NOW calls Gemini (This is the wait)

Loading UI: \"Optimizing to requirements\...\" → \"Calculating scores\...\" → \"Ranking results\...\"

↓

Results appear.

The loading animation appears **after** the user clicks Calculate and **before** results are shown. This is already where your 

calculateResult() does its 

fetch()

 --- you just add a loading overlay there.

**Doubt 3: What If Reviews Are Pure Trash (\"Taj Mahal is beautiful\")?**

This is a **Garbage-in, Garbage-out** problem. Your options:

1.  **AI returns a low score automatically.** If Gemini reads \"Taj Mahal is beautiful\" against the ideal \"Healthy, Tasty juice,\" it cannot find any feature match → it should return \~1 or 2. This is actually correct behavior: an irrelevant review = nearly 0 quality signal.

2.  **Confidence flag.** You can instruct Gemini to return 

{\"score\": 2, \"confidence\": \"low\"}

 instead of just 

2

. If confidence is 

\"low\"

, you surface a warning: *\"⚠️ The AI found this review irrelevant to \'\${featureName}\'. Consider replacing it.\"* --- but still proceed.

3.  (Optional) **Pre-validation prompt.** Before scoring, ask Gemini: \"Is this text relevant to the feature \'\${featureName}\'? Reply YES or NO.\" If NO, ask the user to re-enter.

**Recommended for Phase 1.5:** Option 2 (confidence flag). Simple, does not block the user, and shows transparency in your documentation.

**Doubt 4: Individual Score Per Review, or Comparative Feedback Across All 4?**

**Individual, without comparative context. Here\'s why with your example:**

Ideal: \"Healthy, Tasty juice\"

Review1: \"Very healthy but not tasty\" → Gemini scores: 6

Review2: \"Not healthy\" → Gemini scores: 2

Review3: \"Very tasty\" → Gemini scores: 6

Review4: \"Very Healthy\" → Gemini scores: 8

Gemini gets **one call per product-feature pair.** It sees:

-   featureName

: \"Expert Opinion\"

-   idealDescription

: \"Healthy, Tasty juice\"

-   reviewText

: \"Very healthy but not tasty\"

-   Outputs: 

6

**It does NOT know about Review2, 3, or 4.** Why?

-   **Transparency:** If you send all 4 together and ask for ranks, the AI makes the decision --- which violates Vonnue\'s rule (\"not AI dependent\").

-   **Determinism:** Sending them one-by-one means each score is independent. Your penalty engine then does the comparing --- not the AI.

Think of the AI as a **\"translator.\"** It converts 

\"Very healthy but not tasty\"

 → 

6

. Your engine then calculates 

penalty = max(0, 10 - 6) = 4

. The *comparison* between 4 products is done by your math, not by Gemini.

**Doubt 5: Do You Need an Approval Stage Where the User Verifies AI Scores?**

**This is the most impactful design decision.** Yes, and here is how it works:

If the user clicks **\"🔄 Change\"** on one row, that row turns into the Scale dropdown (Excellent → Poor). The user picks manually, and only that one score is replaced. Then they click \"Confirm & Calculate.\"

**Why this is gold for Vonnue:**

*\"The AI suggests scores, but the human always has final control. This ensures the system is AI-assisted, not AI-dependent.\"*

For 3 products × 3 reviewable features = 9 AI scores → 9 rows in the approval table.

**Doubt 6: Send Context Per Feature or Per All 12 Reviews?**

**Per Feature. Always.** Here\'s the comparison:

**Option A --- All 12 reviews at once:**

-   You send 12 reviews + 3 ideals in one giant prompt.

-   Gemini must figure out which review belongs to which feature.

-   Errors in attribution are unpredictable and untraceable.

-   If one review fails the score, you can\'t retry just that one.

**Option B --- Per Feature (Recommended):**

-   For \"Expert Opinion\" → 1 API call per product (4 calls).

-   Each call has exactly: 

featureName

, 

idealDescription

, 

reviewText

.

-   Clean, atomic, and retryable.

-   Total for your 3-feature, 3-product example: 9 calls (only for \"review\" type features).

**The 9 calls happen in parallel** (

Promise.all

) so the total wait time is the time of the *slowest single call*, not 9× the time.

Want me to update the implementation plan with these decisions baked in, especially the **Approval Stage** (Doubt 5), which is a significant new UI step?

# Antigravity Prompt 30 to Claude : Implement it

Summary Table: Design Decisions for Phase 1.5 Doubt Decision Ideal type matching ✅ Yes, UI enforces same type Loading screen ✅ Yes, between \"Calculate\" click and results Trash reviews ⚠️ Confidence flag + user warning, but proceed Individual vs comparative ✅ Individual (per product-feature pair) Approval stage ✅ Yes, user can override before final calculation Context scope ✅ Per Feature, parallel API calls Want me to update the implementation plan with these decisions baked in, especially the Approval Stage (Doubt 5), which is a significant new UI step? As the next step in our evaluation process, we would like you to complete a take-home assignment. This round is intentionally different from a traditional coding test. As our CEO puts it: "We want to see how you build." This assignment is designed to evaluate: 1. How clearly you document your thinking 2. How you approach ambiguous problems 3. Your system design and architectural decisions 4. How you leverage tools (including AI) 5. Your transparency in the build process Problem Statement: Design and build a "Decision Companion System" that helps a user make better decisions. The system should assist a user in evaluating options for a real-world decision of their choice. Your system must work without relying entirely on an AI model. If AI is used, clearly justify its role and limitations. Examples (you are NOT limited to these): \* Choosing a laptop under a budget \* Selecting the best candidate for a job role \* Deciding where to travel within constraints \* Picking an investment strategy \* Choosing a tech stack for a startup Core Expectations: Your system must: \* Accept multiple options \* Accept criteria (which may have different weights or importance) \* Process and evaluate options against criteria \* Provide a ranked recommendation \* Explain why a particular recommendation was made Beyond this, the design is up to you. You may choose: \* CLI / Web App / API / Desktop tool \* Any programming language \* Any framework \* Simple or advanced logic You define the depth. We are more interested in your thinking than feature count. RESEARCH_LOG.md Include: \* All AI prompts used \* All search queries (including Google searches) \* References that influenced your approach \* What you accepted, rejected, or modified from AI outputs We are not judging you for using AI. # Codex Prompt 86 : changes.md

**Visualizer Idea 2 --- Implementation Spec**

**What to replace**

Replace the existing orb system (dropOrbTo function) entirely. Keep everything else --- platforms, characters, emotions, narrator, sinkPlatform, floatTxt.

**New Layout Zones**

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

│ NARRATOR BAR (existing, unchanged) │

├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

│ MATH ZONE (top \~30% of canvas) │

│ - Shows equation text above each candidate │

│ - Shows laser balls materializing │

├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

│ CHARACTER + PLATFORM ZONE (middle, existing) │

├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

│ VALUES ZONE (below platforms) │

│ - Raw values per candidate always visible │

│ - Ideal value highlighted when criterion active │

├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

│ CONTROL BAR (existing, unchanged) │

└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

**New Constants**

const MATH_ZONE_Y = H \* 0.08; // top of math zone

const BALL_ZONE_Y = H \* 0.22; // where laser balls float

const VALUES_ZONE_Y = GROUND_Y + PLAT_H + 50; // below platform penalty score

**Raw Data to Add to DEMO object**

// Add to DEMO:

raw: {

\"Alice\": { \"Skills\": 85, \"Experience\": 70, \"Culture Fit\": 90 },

\"Bob\": { \"Skills\": 92, \"Experience\": 60, \"Culture Fit\": 65 },

\"Charlie\": { \"Skills\": 75, \"Experience\": 88, \"Culture Fit\": 80 },

},

ideals: { \"Skills\": 90, \"Experience\": 85, \"Culture Fit\": 95 },

// Normalized values (pre-computed, mirrors what backend returns)

normed: {

\"Alice\": { \"Skills\": 58.8, \"Experience\": 100.0, \"Culture Fit\": 100.0 },

\"Bob\": { \"Skills\": 100.0, \"Experience\": 0.0, \"Culture Fit\": 0.0 },

\"Charlie\": { \"Skills\": 0.0, \"Experience\": 88.2, \"Culture Fit\": 57.1 },

},

normedIdeals: { \"Skills\": 88.2, \"Experience\": 58.8, \"Culture Fit\": 80.0 },

**Values Zone (always visible, per candidate)**

Draw below each platform after spawnChars(). Show all feature raw values. When a criterion step begins, highlight the active feature row in that candidate\'s color.

function drawValuesZone(activeFeature = null) {

// For each candidate i:

// For each feature fi:

// text = \`\${feature}: \${DEMO.raw\[candidate\]\[feature\]}\`

// if feature === activeFeature → highlight color, else dim gray

// position: x = CENTERS\[i\], y = VALUES_ZONE_Y + fi \* 18

}

**Ideal Badge in Narrator Bar**

Add a second badge next to criterion-badge:

\<div id=\"ideal-badge\"\>

\<div id=\"ideal-label\"\>IDEAL\</div\>

\<div id=\"ideal-value\"\>---\</div\>

\</div\>

Show/hide same as criterion-badge. Update with DEMO.ideals\[feat\] each criterion step.

**New Function: laserCriterion(fi)**

Replaces stepCriterion. Called same way from nextStep().

SEQUENCE per criterion fi:

1\. Show narrator text + badge + ideal badge

2\. Highlight active feature row in values zone

3\. For each candidate i (one at a time):

PHASE A --- Penalty Ball Materializes:

a\. Show equation text above candidate in math zone:

Line1: \`\${feat}: \${raw} → norm: \${normed}\`

Line2: \`Penalty = max(0, \${normedIdeal} - \${normed}) = \${penalty}\`

b\. Compute ball brightness from penalty (0=transparent, 100=max glow)

c\. Materialize laser ball at BALL_ZONE_Y above CENTERS\[i\]

\- Size: fixed BASE_RADIUS (e.g. 28px) at this stage

\- Color: penalty=0 → transparent + colored border only

penalty\>0 → glowing, higher penalty = brighter/more saturated

\- Use PIXI.Graphics with Pixi filters (BlurFilter for glow effect)

\- Ball pulses gently (scale oscillation via ticker)

d\. await delay(1200)

4\. After all 3 balls materialized --- pause 800ms so user sees all 3

5\. For each candidate i (one at a time):

PHASE B --- Weight Applied, Ball Fires:

a\. Update equation text:

\`Weighted Penalty = \${penalty} × \${weight} = \${weightedPenalty}\`

b\. Ball grows from BASE_RADIUS to WEIGHTED_RADIUS

WEIGHTED_RADIUS = BASE_RADIUS + weight \* 60 (bigger = heavier weight)

Animate scale over 600ms

c\. weightedPenalty value text appears INSIDE the ball

d\. Ball fires DOWN toward character:

\- Animate y from BALL_ZONE_Y to character y over 800ms

\- Easing: accelerate (ease-in)

e\. On impact:

\- If penalty = 0: green tick ✓ appears, no platform sink

\- If penalty \> 0: platform sinks, character shakes

\- Flash effect at impact point

f\. runPenalty\[i\] += weightedPenalty

g\. await updateEmos() (sequential, existing logic)

h\. await delay(400)

6\. Clear math zone text and balls

7\. Narrator reaction (existing logic)

**Laser Ball Visual Spec (Pixi Graphics)**

function makeLaserBall(penalty, maxPenalty) {

const t = Math.min(penalty / maxPenalty, 1); // 0 to 1

// Color: interpolate transparent → orange → red

// t=0: alpha=0, border only (0x4ade80 green border)

// t=0.5: 0xff9900 orange glow

// t=1: 0xff2200 red, intense

const ball = new PIXI.Graphics();

if (t \< 0.01) {

// Zero penalty --- transparent with green border

ball.lineStyle(2.5, 0x4ade80, 0.9);

ball.drawCircle(0, 0, BASE_RADIUS);

} else {

const r = Math.round(255);

const g = Math.round(150 \* (1 - t));

const color = (r \<\< 16) \| (g \<\< 8);

ball.beginFill(color, 0.15 + t \* 0.55);

ball.drawCircle(0, 0, BASE_RADIUS);

ball.endFill();

ball.lineStyle(2, color, 0.9);

ball.drawCircle(0, 0, BASE_RADIUS);

}

// Glow: use PIXI BlurFilter on a separate glow layer

// OR simulate with concentric circles at decreasing alpha

if (t \> 0.1) {

ball.beginFill(color, 0.06); ball.drawCircle(0,0, BASE_RADIUS\*1.6); ball.endFill();

ball.beginFill(color, 0.03); ball.drawCircle(0,0, BASE_RADIUS\*2.2); ball.endFill();

}

return ball;

}

**Pulse Animation (idle while waiting)**

function startPulse(ball) {

let t = 0;

const ticker = () =\> {

t += 0.04;

ball.scale.set(1 + Math.sin(t) \* 0.06);

};

app.ticker.add(ticker);

return ticker; // caller must remove when ball fires

}

**Fire Animation (ball drops to character)**

function fireBall(ball, pulseTicker, targetY) {

return new Promise(resolve =\> {

app.ticker.remove(pulseTicker);

ball.scale.set(1);

const startY = ball.y;

let t = 0;

const ticker = () =\> {

t += 0.018;

const ease = Math.pow(Math.min(t,1), 2); // ease-in (accelerate)

ball.y = startY + (targetY - startY) \* ease;

if (t \>= 1) {

app.ticker.remove(ticker);

fxL.removeChild(ball);

resolve();

}

};

app.ticker.add(ticker);

});

}

# Codex Prompt 93 : CHANGES_fireball.md

**Fireball System --- Codex Implementation Spec**

**Asset Location**

frontend/sprites/fireballs/

fire_ball_side_small/imgs/ img_0.png ... img_29.png (30 frames)

fire_ball_side_medium/imgs/ img_0.png ... img_29.png (30 frames)

fireball_high_speed_side_small/imgs/ img_0.png ... img_39.png (40 frames)

meteor_side_medium/imgs/ img_0.png ... img_29.png (30 frames)

fire_ball_blue_side_small/imgs/ img_0.png ... img_34.png (35 frames)

All frames are 400x400px transparent PNG.

**Penalty → Fireball Type Mapping**

function getFireballType(penalty) {

if (penalty \< 0.01) return null; // zero → green ring only

if (penalty \<= 25) return \'fire_ball_side_small\';

if (penalty \<= 50) return \'fire_ball_side_medium\';

if (penalty \<= 75) return \'fireball_high_speed_side_small\';

return \'meteor_side_medium\';

}

function getFrameCount(type) {

if (type === \'fireball_high_speed_side_small\') return 40;

if (type === \'fire_ball_blue_side_small\') return 35;

return 30;

}

**Preload All Fireball Textures**

Add to loadTextures() --- load all frame arrays into:

const fireballTextures = {

fire_ball_side_small: \[\],

fire_ball_side_medium: \[\],

fireball_high_speed_side_small: \[\],

meteor_side_medium: \[\],

fire_ball_blue_side_small: \[\],

};

// In loadTextures(), for each type:

for (let f = 0; f \< frameCount; f++) {

const path = \`sprites/fireballs/\${type}/imgs/img\_\${f}.png\`;

fireballTextures\[type\].push(await PIXI.Assets.load(path));

}

**makeLaserBall(penalty) --- FULL REPLACEMENT**

Replace the existing makeLaserBall entirely.

function makeLaserBall(penalty) {

const container = new PIXI.Container();

const type = getFireballType(penalty);

if (!type) {

// Zero penalty --- green glowing ring only, no fireball sprite

const ring = new PIXI.Graphics();

ring.lineStyle(3, 0x4ade80, 0.9);

ring.drawCircle(0, 0, 28);

// Outer soft glow ring

ring.lineStyle(8, 0x4ade80, 0.15);

ring.drawCircle(0, 0, 36);

container.addChild(ring);

container.\_isRing = true;

return container;

}

const frames = fireballTextures\[type\];

const anim = new PIXI.AnimatedSprite(frames);

anim.anchor.set(0.5, 0.5);

// Rotate so side-facing fireball points downward (trail goes up)

anim.rotation = Math.PI / 2;

// Scale: base size proportional to penalty intensity

const t = Math.min(penalty / 100, 1);

const baseScale = 0.18 + t \* 0.22; // 0.18 at low penalty → 0.40 at max

anim.scale.set(baseScale);

// Animation speed: same for all (size conveys intensity, not speed)

anim.animationSpeed = 0.4;

anim.loop = true;

anim.play();

container.addChild(anim);

container.\_anim = anim;

container.\_isRing = false;

return container;

}

**scaleBallToWeight(ball, weight)**

After Phase A (penalty ball materialized), grow ball to weighted size:

function scaleBallToWeight(ball, weight, penalty) {

return new Promise(resolve =\> {

if (ball.\_isRing) { resolve(); return; }

const anim = ball.\_anim;

const t = Math.min(penalty / 100, 1);

const baseScale = 0.18 + t \* 0.22;

const weightedScale = baseScale + weight \* 0.35; // heavier weight = bigger fireball

const startScale = anim.scale.x;

let tick = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

tick += 0.025;

const ease = 1 - Math.pow(1 - Math.min(tick, 1), 3);

const s = startScale + (weightedScale - startScale) \* ease;

anim.scale.set(s);

if (tick \>= 1) { app.ticker.remove(fn); resolve(); }

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

});

}

**startPulse(ball) --- idle float animation**

function startPulse(ball) {

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.035;

ball.y += Math.sin(t) \* 0.4; // gentle vertical float

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

return fn; // caller stores and removes this reference

}

**fireBall(ball, pulseFn, targetY) --- drop animation**

function fireBall(ball, pulseFn, targetY) {

return new Promise(resolve =\> {

app.ticker.remove(pulseFn);

const startY = ball.y;

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.02;

const ease = Math.pow(Math.min(t, 1), 2); // ease-in, accelerates downward

ball.y = startY + (targetY - startY) \* ease;

if (t \>= 1) {

app.ticker.remove(fn);

fxL.removeChild(ball);

if (ball.\_anim) ball.\_anim.stop();

resolve();

}

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

});

}

**Impact Flash**

function flashImpact(x, y, penalty) {

const color = penalty \< 0.01 ? 0x4ade80 : penalty \< 50 ? 0xff9900 : 0xff2200;

const flash = new PIXI.Graphics();

flash.beginFill(color, 0.7);

flash.drawCircle(x, y, 40);

flash.endFill();

fxL.addChild(flash);

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.06;

flash.alpha = 1 - t;

flash.scale.set(1 + t \* 0.8);

if (t \>= 1) { app.ticker.remove(fn); fxL.removeChild(flash); }

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

}

**laserCriterion(fi) --- Full Sequence**

Replace existing stepCriterion / laserCriterion with this exact sequence:

1\. setNarrator(narration\[fi\], \'explaining\')

2\. showBadge(feat, weight) + showIdealBadge(DEMO.ideals\[feat\])

3\. drawValuesZone(feat) ← highlights active feature row

4\. await delay(1000)

── PHASE A: Materialize balls one by one ──

5\. For i = 0 to N-1:

a\. penalty = DEMO.detailed_breakdown\[candidate\]\[feat\].penalty (raw penalty, NOT weighted)

b\. Show math text for this candidate (left-aligned block, see Math Text spec below)

Line 1: \`\${feat}: \${raw} → norm: \${normed}\`

Line 2: \`Penalty = max(0, \${normedIdeal.toFixed(1)} − \${normed.toFixed(1)}) = \${penalty.toFixed(1)}\`

c\. ball = makeLaserBall(penalty)

d\. ball.x = CENTERS\[i\]

e\. ball.y = BALL_ZONE_Y

f\. fxL.addChild(ball)

g\. pulseFns\[i\] = startPulse(ball)

h\. balls\[i\] = ball

i\. await delay(1400) ← user reads the math, sees ball appear

6\. await delay(1000) ← all 3 balls visible, pause so user sees them together

── PHASE B: Apply weight, fire one by one ──

7\. For i = 0 to N-1:

a\. weightedPenalty = DEMO.detailed_breakdown\[candidate\]\[feat\].weighted_penalty

b\. Update math text line 2 for this candidate:

\`Weighted = \${penalty.toFixed(1)} × \${weight.toFixed(2)} = \${weightedPenalty.toFixed(1)}\`

c\. await scaleBallToWeight(balls\[i\], weight, penalty) ← ball grows

d\. await delay(600)

e\. targetY = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] - CHAR_H \* 0.1

f\. await fireBall(balls\[i\], pulseFns\[i\], targetY)

g\. flashImpact(CENTERS\[i\], targetY, weightedPenalty)

h\. runPenalty\[i\] += weightedPenalty

i\. if (weightedPenalty \< 0.01): show green tick floatTxt at impact point

j\. else: await sinkPlatform(i, (weightedPenalty/100)\*MAX_SINK)

k\. await updateEmos() ← sequential emotion update

l\. await delay(500)

8\. clearMathTexts()

9\. Narrator reaction based on current leader

10\. await delay(600)

// Math zone: fixed left column

# Codex Prompt 100 : New Fixes

**Visual Fixes 5-9 --- Codex Spec**

**Fix 5 --- Math Text in Rectangular Box Per Candidate**

**Current**

Math text floats centered above each candidate column, no background.

**Required**

Each candidate gets a dedicated rectangular box drawn in fxL, centered above their column. Box appears when that candidate\'s math text appears, stays until clearMathTexts() is called.

// Box spec:

// width: SLOT_W \* 0.72

// height: 72

// x: CENTERS\[i\] - boxW/2

// y: MATH_ZONE_Y - 8

// Fill: rgba(10, 10, 40, 0.82) → 0x0a0a28, alpha 0.82

// Border: 1.5px, color = CHAR_COLORS\[i\], alpha 0.7

// Border radius: 8

// Inside box:

// Line 1 (top): e.g. \"Skills: 85 → norm: 58.8\"

// font: Courier New, 12px, fill: 0xaaaaff

// x: CENTERS\[i\], anchor (0.5, 0), y: MATH_ZONE_Y + 4

// Line 2 (bottom): e.g. \"Penalty = max(0, 88.2 − 58.8) = 29.4\"

// font: Courier New, 12px, fill: 0xffffff

// x: CENTERS\[i\], anchor (0.5, 0), y: MATH_ZONE_Y + 26

// Line 3 (weighted, appears in Phase B): \"Weighted = 29.4 × 0.50 = 14.7\"

// font: Courier New, 12px, fill: CHAR_COLORS\[i\]

// x: CENTERS\[i\], anchor (0.5, 0), y: MATH_ZONE_Y + 48

Store all box graphics and text objects in mathBoxes array (indexed by charIndex). clearMathTexts() removes all of them from fxL.

**Fix 6 --- Calculations and IDEAL Stay Until Next Button Click**

**Current**

clearMathTexts() is called at end of laserCriterion() automatically after all orbs fire.

**Required**

Do NOT call clearMathTexts() at end of laserCriterion(). Instead call clearMathTexts() at the VERY START of the next laserCriterion() call (before new boxes appear). Also call it at start of stepNorm() and at start of showWinner().

This means after all 3 orbs have fired and hit, the math boxes + IDEAL text stay visible. User reads them. When they click \"Apply: Experience →\", THEN they disappear and new ones appear.

**Implementation**

In laserCriterion(fi):

-   Line 1 of function body: clearMathTexts() ← clears PREVIOUS criterion\'s boxes

-   Remove any existing clearMathTexts() call at the END of the function

In stepNorm():

-   Add clearMathTexts() at start

In showWinner():

-   Add clearMathTexts() at start

**Fix 7 --- \"No Penalty\" Text: Static, No Animation, No Orb Hit**

-   Text is STATIC --- no pulse, no movement

-   NO fire animation, NO impact flash, NO platform interaction

-   Text stays until clearMathTexts() (same as Fix 6)

-   Still call runPenalty\[i\] += 0 and updateEmos() to keep logic consistent

**Implementation in laserCriterion Phase A + B**

if (weightedPenalty \< 0.01) {

// Show static \"No Penalty\" box --- already done in Phase A

// Phase B: skip all animation, just update state

runPenalty\[i\] += 0;

}

**Fix 8 --- Penalty Value Fades In as Text After Impact, Stays Visible**

**Current**

Penalty value appears as a floating text that drifts upward and fades (floatTxt).

**Required**

After the fireball hits, the weighted penalty value appears as a STATIC label below the platform. It fades IN (not out), then stays until clearMathTexts().

Style:

// Text: \`-\${weightedPenalty.toFixed(1)}\` e.g. \"-14.7\"

// Font: bold, 22px, fill: CHAR_COLORS\[i\] (platform color)

// Position: x = CENTERS\[i\], y = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] + PLAT_H + 30

// anchor: (0.5, 0)

// Fade in over 400ms (alpha 0 → 1)

// Add to fxL, store in mathBoxes so clearMathTexts() removes it

Implementation:

function showPenaltyLabel(charIndex, weightedPenalty) {

return new Promise(resolve =\> {

const txt = new PIXI.Text(\`-\${weightedPenalty.toFixed(1)}\`, {

fontFamily: \'-apple-system, sans-serif\',

fontSize: 22,

fontWeight: \'bold\',

fill: CHAR_COLORS\[charIndex\],

dropShadow: true,

dropShadowColor: 0x000000,

dropShadowDistance: 2,

});

txt.anchor.set(0.5, 0);

txt.x = CENTERS\[charIndex\];

txt.y = GROUND_Y + platSink\[charIndex\] + PLAT_H + 30;

txt.alpha = 0;

fxL.addChild(txt);

mathBoxes.push(txt); // so clearMathTexts removes it

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.04;

txt.alpha = Math.min(t, 1);

if (t \>= 1) { app.ticker.remove(fn); resolve(); }

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

});

}

Call await showPenaltyLabel(i, weightedPenalty) in Phase B AFTER flashImpact and sinkPlatform. Also remove the existing floatTxt call that shows the penalty value (if any).

**Required**

Penalty → fireball type mapping stays the same (already correct). But also map penalty → initial scale directly:

// In makeLaserBall, replace current baseScale calculation:

const t = Math.min(penalty / 100, 1);

// No further scaling after this. Ball appears at final size immediately.

Remove scaleBallToWeight() call from Phase B entirely. Remove the await scaleBallToWeight(\...) and await delay(600) after it. Ball appears at correct size in Phase A and stays that size until it fires.

The blue fireball (fire_ball_blue_side_small) = reserved for highest penalty tier:

function getFireballType(penalty) {

if (penalty \< 0.01) return null;

if (penalty \<= 20) return \'fire_ball_side_small\';

if (penalty \<= 45) return \'fire_ball_side_medium\';

if (penalty \<= 70) return \'fireball_high_speed_side_small\';

if (penalty \<= 88) return \'meteor_side_medium\';

return \'fire_ball_blue_side_small\'; // highest penalty = blue, largest

}

**Both elements must update Y position when platform sinks.** In sinkPlatform(), after each tick update, reposition these elements. Best approach: store them in per-character arrays penaltyLabels\[i\] and valueBoxContainers\[i\] and call a updateFloatingElements() function inside the sinkPlatform ticker.

function updateFloatingElements() {

for (let i = 0; i \< N; i++) {

if (penaltyLabels\[i\]) {

penaltyLabels\[i\].y = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] + PLAT_H + 10;

}

if (valueBoxContainers\[i\]) {

valueBoxContainers\[i\].y = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] - CHAR_H \* 0.45;

}

}

}

**Fix 11 --- Reduce Blue Fireball Max Scale**

**Current**

fire_ball_blue_side_small uses same scale formula as others: baseScale = 0.32 + t \* 0.45 at t≈1 gives \~0.77

**Required**

Cap blue fireball scale so it doesn\'t overlap the character:

function makeLaserBall(penalty) {

const type = getFireballType(penalty);

const t = Math.min(penalty / 100, 1);

let baseScale = 0.32 + t \* 0.45;

// Cap blue (highest tier) to prevent overlap

if (type === \'fire_ball_blue_side_small\') {

baseScale = Math.min(baseScale, 0.52);

}

// \...rest unchanged

}

const penaltyLabelObjs = \[null, null, null\]; // LEFT penalty text per candidate

**New Function: showValuesBox(charIndex, activeFeature)**

Called at START of each laserCriterion (Phase A, for each candidate). Creates the right-side values box for candidate i.

function showValuesBox(charIndex, activeFeature) {

// Remove existing if any

if (valueBoxObjs\[charIndex\]) {

fxL.removeChild(valueBoxObjs\[charIndex\]);

valueBoxObjs\[charIndex\] = null;

}

const cx = CENTERS\[charIndex\];

const torsoY = GROUND_Y + platSink\[charIndex\] - CHAR_H \* 0.5;

const BOX_W = SLOT_W \* 0.28;

const BOX_H = 68;

const BOX_X = cx + SLOT_W \* 0.18; // right of character

const BOX_Y = torsoY - BOX_H / 2;

const container = new PIXI.Container();

container.\_charIndex = charIndex;

// Box background

const box = new PIXI.Graphics();

box.beginFill(0x0a0a28, 0.88);

box.drawRoundedRect(0, 0, BOX_W, BOX_H, 7);

box.endFill();

box.lineStyle(1.5, CHAR_COLORS\[charIndex\], 0.65);

box.drawRoundedRect(0, 0, BOX_W, BOX_H, 7);

container.addChild(box);

// Three value rows

const candidate = DEMO.candidates\[charIndex\];

const labels = \[\'S\', \'E\', \'C\'\];

const featKeys = DEMO.features; // \[\'Skills\', \'Experience\', \'Culture Fit\'\]

for (let fi = 0; fi \< 3; fi++) {

const feat = featKeys\[fi\];

const val = DEMO.raw\[candidate\]\[feat\];

const isActive = feat === activeFeature;

const rowTxt = new PIXI.Text(\`\${labels\[fi\]} : \${val}\`, {

fontFamily: \'Courier New\',

fontSize: 13,

fontWeight: isActive ? \'bold\' : \'normal\',

fill: isActive ? CHAR_COLORS\[charIndex\] : 0x9999bb,

dropShadow: false,

});

rowTxt.x = 10;

rowTxt.y = 8 + fi \* 20;

container.addChild(rowTxt);

}

container.x = BOX_X;

container.y = BOX_Y;

fxL.addChild(container);

valueBoxObjs\[charIndex\] = container;

}

**New Function: showPenaltyLabel(charIndex, weightedPenalty)**

Called AFTER fireball hits (Phase B, after sinkPlatform). Creates left-side penalty label for candidate i. Fades in over 400ms then stays static.

function showPenaltyLabel(charIndex, weightedPenalty) {

return new Promise(resolve =\> {

// Remove existing if any

if (penaltyLabelObjs\[charIndex\]) {

fxL.removeChild(penaltyLabelObjs\[charIndex\]);

penaltyLabelObjs\[charIndex\] = null;

}

const cx = CENTERS\[charIndex\];

const torsoY = GROUND_Y + platSink\[charIndex\] - CHAR_H \* 0.5;

const txt = new PIXI.Text(\`-\${weightedPenalty.toFixed(1)}\`, {

fontFamily: \'-apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, sans-serif\',

fontSize: 24,

fontWeight: \'bold\',

fill: CHAR_COLORS\[charIndex\],

dropShadow: true,

dropShadowColor: 0x000000,

dropShadowDistance: 2,

});

txt.anchor.set(1.0, 0.5); // right-aligned anchor

txt.x = cx - SLOT_W \* 0.18; // left of character

txt.y = torsoY;

txt.alpha = 0;

txt.\_charIndex = charIndex;

fxL.addChild(txt);

penaltyLabelObjs\[charIndex\] = txt;

// Fade in

let t = 0;

const fn = () =\> {

t += 0.04;

txt.alpha = Math.min(t, 1);

if (t \>= 1) { app.ticker.remove(fn); resolve(); }

};

app.ticker.add(fn);

});

}

**updateFloatingElements() --- Called Every Sink Tick**

function updateFloatingElements() {

for (let i = 0; i \< N; i++) {

const torsoY = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] - CHAR_H \* 0.5;

// Move penalty label (left side)

if (penaltyLabelObjs\[i\]) {

penaltyLabelObjs\[i\].y = torsoY;

}

// Move values box (right side)

if (valueBoxObjs\[i\]) {

const BOX_H = 68;

valueBoxObjs\[i\].y = torsoY - BOX_H / 2;

}

}

}

Call updateFloatingElements():

1.  Inside sinkPlatform() ticker on every tick (after updating platSink\[i\])

2.  Inside redraw() function

**Fix 6 --- Auto-Follow Camera (gameWorld Container)**

**Structural Change: wrap all layers in gameWorld**

**Camera state:**

let cameraY = 0; // current gameWorld.y offset (negative = moved up)

let cameraTargetY = 0;

**updateCamera() --- called every frame in app.ticker**

app.ticker.add(() =\> {

// Smooth camera follow

if (Math.abs(gameWorld.y - cameraTargetY) \> 0.5) {

gameWorld.y += (cameraTargetY - gameWorld.y) \* 0.08;

} else {

gameWorld.y = cameraTargetY;

}

});

**recalcCameraTarget() --- called after each platSink update**

function recalcCameraTarget() {

// Find the lowest point across all candidates

// Lowest point = running total text position = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] + PLAT_H + 40

let lowestY = 0;

for (let i = 0; i \< N; i++) {

const bottom = GROUND_Y + platSink\[i\] + PLAT_H + 50;

if (bottom \> lowestY) lowestY = bottom;

}

// If lowest point exceeds visible canvas minus padding:

const margin = 50;

if (lowestY \> H - margin) {

cameraTargetY = -(lowestY - (H - margin));

}

// Never go above 0 (don\'t scroll up beyond start)

cameraTargetY = Math.min(cameraTargetY, 0);

}

**Call recalcCameraTarget() in sinkPlatform ticker:**

Inside sinkPlatform() ticker, after updating platSink\[charIndex\]:

recalcCameraTarget(); // ← ADD THIS every tick

**Reset camera on restart:**

In restartVisualization():

cameraY = 0;

cameraTargetY = 0;

gameWorld.y = 0;

**Important: fxL is inside gameWorld**

Since fxL is now inside gameWorld, all fireball positions, math boxes, penalty labels, values boxes --- their Y coordinates are already in gameWorld local space. No coordinate changes needed.

**Fix 7 --- Normalization Step: Boxes Instead of Floating Text**

Replace stepNorm() content entirely:

async function stepNorm() {

clearMathTexts();

setNarrator(\"Normalization compresses all raw scores to a 0--100 scale so every criterion is judged fairly.\", \'explaining\');

hideBadge();

// Show one normalization box per candidate

for (let i = 0; i \< N; i++) {

const candidate = DEMO.candidates\[i\];

const BOX_W = SLOT_W \* 0.52;

const BOX_H = 82;

const cx = CENTERS\[i\];

const cy = GROUND_Y - CHAR_H \* 0.6; // above character

const container = new PIXI.Container();

// Box background

const box = new PIXI.Graphics();

box.beginFill(0x0a0a28, 0.9);

box.drawRoundedRect(0, 0, BOX_W, BOX_H, 8);

box.endFill();

box.lineStyle(1.5, CHAR_COLORS\[i\], 0.6);

box.drawRoundedRect(0, 0, BOX_W, BOX_H, 8);

container.addChild(box);

// Three normalization rows

for (let fi = 0; fi \< DEMO.features.length; fi++) {

const feat = DEMO.features\[fi\];

const raw = DEMO.raw\[candidate\]\[feat\];

const norm = DEMO.normed\[candidate\]\[feat\];

const rowTxt = new PIXI.Text(\`\${feat}: \${raw} → norm: \${norm.toFixed(1)}\`, {

fontFamily: \'Courier New\',

fontSize: 12,

fill: 0xaaaaff,

dropShadow: false,

});

rowTxt.x = 10;

rowTxt.y = 8 + fi \* 24;

container.addChild(rowTxt);

}

container.x = cx - BOX_W / 2;

container.y = cy - BOX_H / 2;

fxL.addChild(container);

mathBoxes.push(container);

}

// Stay visible --- do NOT clearMathTexts here

// Cleared at start of next laserCriterion (Fix 6 from previous spec)

document.getElementById(\'next-btn\').textContent = \`Apply: \${DEMO.features\[0\]} →\`;

}

**Add JS Functions**

function manualScroll(deltaPx) {

// deltaPx negative = scroll up (camera moves up = scene moves down visually)

// deltaPx positive = scroll down

cameraTargetY -= deltaPx;

// Clamp: never scroll above origin, never scroll below max sink

const maxDown = -(MAX_SINK \* 1.2);

cameraTargetY = Math.max(cameraTargetY, maxDown);

cameraTargetY = Math.min(cameraTargetY, 0);

}

function scrollToTop() {

cameraTargetY = 0;

// Smooth ticker already handles animation back to 0

}

**Auto Pan To Top After All Camera Movements Done**

After the last criterion\'s Phase B completes (all 3 candidates processed), add at the END of laserCriterion(fi) when fi === DEMO.features.length - 1:

// After last criterion narrator reaction + delay:

if (fi === DEMO.features.length - 1) {

scrollToTop(); // gently pan back to top so winner reveal looks clean

await delay(900); // wait for camera to finish panning

}

// REMOVE:

const cy = GROUND_Y - CHAR_H \* 0.6;

// REPLACE WITH:

const cy = MATH_ZONE_Y + BOX_H / 2 + 10;

This places all 3 normalization boxes in the top information zone (same area as math equation boxes during criteria), one per candidate column centered at CENTERS\[i\].

const BOX_H = 88; // was 82

# Codex Prompt 119 : Integrating prototype with real data

Here\'s what the spec covers and why each decision was made:

3 files, clear separation of concerns:

decisionLogic.js --- The only tricky part is that d\[i\]\[y\] gets overwritten by the penalty value inside the scoring loop. So the spec captures normedValues as a snapshot before that loop runs, not after. Miss that timing and you\'d store penalty scores instead of normalized values --- a silent bug that would be hard to trace.

server.js --- One line addition: raw: products_data. The normed and normedIdeals fields come through automatically via \...result spread since they\'re now returned by calculateDecision().

script.js --- Uses sessionStorage rather than URL params or localStorage because the data can be large (many products × many features) and sessionStorage is tab-scoped so it auto-cleans on tab close. The visualizer consumes and immediately deletes the key (removeItem) so a manual reload of the visualizer falls back to the demo cleanly.

visualizer_prototype.html --- The loadDemoData() pattern means the fallback demo is preserved exactly, the file stays standalone-runnable, and real data is opt-in. The dynamic N changes are minimal --- most loops already used N, the main fixes are the array initializations and the hardcoded \<3\> inside showValuesBox. **\# CHANGES_real.md**

**\## Integrate Visualizer with Real \`/api/calculate\` Response Data**

*\*Spec for Codex. Apply changes precisely. DO NOT change anything not listed here.\**

\-\--

**\## Overview**

The visualizer at \`frontend/visualizer_prototype.html\` currently uses a hardcoded \`DEMO\`

object. The goal is to make it consume **\*\*real data\*\*** passed from \`script.js\` after a

successful \`/api/calculate\` response.

Three files are modified:

\| File \| Change \|

\|\-\-\-\-\--\|\-\-\-\-\-\-\--\|

\| \`backend/decisionLogic.js\` \| Return \`raw\`, \`normed\`, \`normedIdeals\` in \`calculateDecision()\` \|

\| \`backend/server.js\` \| Forward those fields in the \`/api/calculate\` response \|

\| \`frontend/script.js\` \| After results, add \"Animate Result 🎬\" button; pass data to visualizer via \`sessionStorage\` \|

\| \`frontend/visualizer_prototype.html\` \| On load, read \`sessionStorage\`; if present replace \`DEMO\`; otherwise keep hardcoded DEMO \|

\-\--

**\## CHANGE 1 --- \`backend/decisionLogic.js\`**

**\### Where: inside \`calculateDecision()\` function**

The function currently builds \`d\` (normalized values), \`norm_req_list\` (normalized ideals),

\`agg_sum\`, and \`detailed_breakdown\`, then returns them.

We need to **\*\*capture intermediate normalized values\*\*** before they get overwritten by penalty

scores, and return them.

**\### Step 1A --- Capture \`normedValues\` before penalty overwrites \`d\`**

Find this block (it comes just after the second normalization loop, before \`agg_sum = {}\`):

\`\`\`js

  const agg_sum = {};

  const detailed_breakdown = {};

  for (const i in d) {

    let tsum = 0;

    detailed_breakdown\[i\] = {};

    for (let x = 0; x \< f_list.length; x++) {

      const y = f_list\[x\];

      let penalty;

      \...

      d\[i\]\[y\] = penalty;   // ← THIS LINE overwrites the normalized value with penalty

\`\`\`

**\*\*Before\*\*** the \`agg_sum = {}\` line, add:

\`\`\`js

  // Snapshot normalized values before penalty calculation overwrites d

  const normedValues = {};

  for (const p in d) {

    normedValues\[p\] = {};

    for (const f of f_list) {

      normedValues\[p\]\[f\] = parseFloat(d\[p\]\[f\].toFixed(4));

    }

  }

\`\`\`

**\### Step 1B --- Build \`normedIdeals\` map**

Immediately after the \`norm_req_list\` array is fully built (after the for loop that pushes

to it), add:

\`\`\`js

  // Build named map of normalized ideal values

  const normedIdeals = {};

  for (let i = 0; i \< f_list.length; i++) {

    normedIdeals\[f_list\[i\]\] = parseFloat(norm_req_list\[i\].toFixed(4));

  }

\`\`\`

**\### Step 1C --- Return the new fields**

Find the \`return {\` statement at the end of \`calculateDecision()\`. It currently returns:

\`\`\`js

  return {

    winner: tie.length === 1 ? tie\[0\] : null,

    tie,

    ranking,

    agg_sum,

    detailed_breakdown,

    weights,

    features: f_list,

    directions: high_or_low,

  };

\`\`\`

Change it to:

\`\`\`js

  return {

    winner: tie.length === 1 ? tie\[0\] : null,

    tie,

    ranking,

    agg_sum,

    detailed_breakdown,

    weights,

    features: f_list,

    directions: high_or_low,

    normed: normedValues,       // { ProductName: { FeatureName: 0-100 } }

    normedIdeals,               // { FeatureName: 0-100 }

  };

\`\`\`

**\### DO NOT CHANGE in decisionLogic.js:**

\- \`preprocessInputs()\`

\- \`extractScoreFromText()\`

\- \`generateExplanation()\`

\- \`build4Styles()\`

\- \`SCALE_MAP\`

\- Any explanation builder functions

\-\--

**\## CHANGE 2 --- \`backend/server.js\`**

**\### Where: inside \`POST /api/calculate\` handler**

The handler currently calls \`calculateDecision()\` and spreads the result:

\`\`\`js

    res.json({

      \...result,

      explanation,

      explanation_source: source,

      explanation_styles: styles,

    });

\`\`\`

The spread \`\...result\` will automatically include the new \`normed\` and \`normedIdeals\`

fields once Change 1 is applied. **\*\*No additional code needed here.\*\***

However, we also need to pass \`raw\` (the original user-entered values) so the visualizer

can display them. \`products_data\` is already available in the handler scope as it comes

from \`req.body\`.

Change the \`res.json(\...)\` call to:

\`\`\`js

    res.json({

      \...result,

      explanation,

      explanation_source: source,

      explanation_styles: styles,

      raw: products_data,   // original user-entered values, shape: { ProductName: { FeatureName: value } }

    });

\`\`\`

**\### DO NOT CHANGE in server.js:**

\- \`/api/preprocess\` route

\- \`app.use(express.static(\...))\` line

\- \`app.listen(\...)\` line

\- Any import/require statements

\-\--

**\## CHANGE 3 --- \`frontend/script.js\`**

**\### Where: inside \`displayResults(result)\` function**

At the very end of \`displayResults()\`, just before \`container.innerHTML = html\`, the

function sets \`container.innerHTML = html\`. We need to:

1\. Store the full result in \`sessionStorage\` (serialized as JSON) under key

   \`\"visualizerData\"\`.

2\. Append an \"Animate Result 🎬\" button to \`html\` that opens the visualizer.

**\*\*Find\*\*** the line that reads:

\`\`\`js

    container.innerHTML = html;

\`\`\`

**\*\*Replace it with:\*\***

\`\`\`js

    // Store result for visualizer

    try {

      sessionStorage.setItem(\'visualizerData\', JSON.stringify({

        candidates: result.ranking.map(r =\> r.product),

        features: result.features,

        weights: result.weights,

        raw: result.raw,

        normed: result.normed,

        normedIdeals: result.normedIdeals,

        ideals: buildRawIdealsMap(result),

        detailed_breakdown: result.detailed_breakdown,

        ranking: result.ranking,

        winner: result.winner,

        explanation: result.explanation,

      }));

    } catch(e) {

      console.warn(\'sessionStorage not available:\', e);

    }

    html += \`

      \<div style=\"margin-top: 24px; text-align: center;\"\>

        \<button onclick=\"openVisualizer()\" class=\"btn-primary\" style=\"font-size:1.1rem; padding: 14px 32px;\"\>

          🎬 Animate Result

        \</button\>

        \<p class=\"hint\" style=\"margin-top: 8px;\"\>Watch the decision play out step-by-step\</p\>

      \</div\>

    \`;

    container.innerHTML = html;

\`\`\`

**\### Add \`buildRawIdealsMap()\` helper function**

Add this new function anywhere in \`script.js\` (suggest: just before \`displayResults\`):

\`\`\`js

// Builds { FeatureName: rawIdealValue } from state.ideals + state.featureNames

// Used to populate the visualizer\'s ideals display

function buildRawIdealsMap(result) {

  const map = {};

  state.featureNames.forEach((name, i) =\> {

    map\[name\] = state.ideals\[i\];

  });

  return map;

}

\`\`\`

**\### Add \`openVisualizer()\` function**

Add this function anywhere in \`script.js\` (suggest: just after \`buildRawIdealsMap\`):

\`\`\`js

function openVisualizer() {

  window.open(\'/visualizer_prototype.html\', \'\_blank\');

}

\`\`\`

**\### DO NOT CHANGE in script.js:**

\- Any step navigation functions (\`showStep\`, \`goBack\`, \`resetForm\`)

\- \`calculateResult()\`, \`runCalculate()\`, \`confirmApproval()\`, \`applyOverride()\`

**\## CHANGE 4 --- \`frontend/visualizer_prototype.html\`**

**\### Where: the \`// ── DEMO DATA ──\` block and \`init()\` function**

This is the most significant change. The visualizer currently has a hardcoded \`DEMO\`

object at the top of the \`\<script\>\` tag. We need it to:

1\. On load, check \`sessionStorage\` for \`\"visualizerData\"\`

2\. If found → parse it and use as \`DEMO\`, then clear the key

3\. If NOT found → keep the existing hardcoded \`DEMO\` as fallback (so the demo still

   works standalone)

**\### Step 4A --- Wrap DEMO in a function and add loader**

**\*\*Find\*\*** the block that starts with:

\`\`\`js

// ── DEMO DATA ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

const DEMO = {

  candidates: \[\"Alice\", \"Bob\", \"Charlie\"\],

  \...

};

\`\`\`

**\*\*Replace the entire \`const DEMO = { \... };\` block\*\*** (from \`// ── DEMO DATA\` comment through

the closing \`};\`) with:

\`\`\`js

// ── DEMO DATA (fallback when no real data is available) ────────────────────

const DEMO_FALLBACK = {

  candidates: \[\"Alice\", \"Bob\", \"Charlie\"\],

  features:   \[\"Skills\", \"Experience\", \"Culture Fit\"\],

  weights:    \[0.5, 0.3, 0.2\],

  raw: {

    \"Alice\":   { \"Skills\":85, \"Experience\":70, \"Culture Fit\":90 },

    \"Bob\":     { \"Skills\":92, \"Experience\":60, \"Culture Fit\":65 },

    \"Charlie\": { \"Skills\":75, \"Experience\":88, \"Culture Fit\":80 },

  },

  ideals: { \"Skills\":90, \"Experience\":85, \"Culture Fit\":95 },

  normed: {

    \"Alice\":   { \"Skills\":58.8,  \"Experience\":100.0, \"Culture Fit\":100.0 },

    \"Bob\":     { \"Skills\":100.0, \"Experience\":0.0,   \"Culture Fit\":0.0   },

    \"Charlie\": { \"Skills\":0.0,   \"Experience\":88.2,  \"Culture Fit\":57.1  },

  },

  normedIdeals: { \"Skills\":88.2, \"Experience\":58.8, \"Culture Fit\":80.0 },

  detailed_breakdown: {

    \"Alice\":   { \"Skills\":{ penalty:0,     weighted_penalty:0    }, \"Experience\":{ penalty:24.07, weighted_penalty:7.22 }, \"Culture Fit\":{ penalty:0,  weighted_penalty:0   } },

    \"Bob\":     { \"Skills\":{ penalty:0,     weighted_penalty:0    }, \"Experience\":{ penalty:100,   weighted_penalty:30   }, \"Culture Fit\":{ penalty:100,weighted_penalty:20  } },

    \"Charlie\": { \"Skills\":{ penalty:40.6,  weighted_penalty:20.3 }, \"Experience\":{ penalty:0,     weighted_penalty:0    }, \"Culture Fit\":{ penalty:40, weighted_penalty:8   } },

  },

  ranking: \[

    { rank:1, product:\"Alice\",   score:7.22 },

    { rank:2, product:\"Charlie\", score:28.3 },

    { rank:3, product:\"Bob\",     score:50.0 },

  \],

  winner: \"Alice\",

  explanation: \"Alice wins with the lowest total penalty. Her exceptional Skills (weight 50%) keep her ahead despite a moderate Experience gap. Bob\'s strength is undermined by poor Experience and Culture Fit. Charlie falls short in Skills --- the most critical criterion.\",

};

// ── LOAD REAL DATA or fall back to demo ────────────────────────────────────

function loadDemoData() {

  try {

    const stored = sessionStorage.getItem(\'visualizerData\');

    if (stored) {

      sessionStorage.removeItem(\'visualizerData\'); // consume once

      const d = JSON.parse(stored);

      // Validate minimum required fields

      if (

        Array.isArray(d.candidates) && d.candidates.length \>= 2 &&

        Array.isArray(d.features)   && d.features.length \>= 1 &&

        Array.isArray(d.weights)    &&

        d.raw && d.normed && d.normedIdeals &&

        d.detailed_breakdown && d.ranking && d.winner

      ) {

        console.log(\'\[Visualizer\] Using real data for:\', d.candidates);

        return d;

      }

    }

  } catch(e) {

    console.warn(\'\[Visualizer\] sessionStorage read failed:\', e);

  }

  console.log(\'\[Visualizer\] Using fallback DEMO data\');

  return DEMO_FALLBACK;

}

const DEMO = loadDemoData();

\`\`\`

const ALL_CHAR_COLORS = \[0x667eea, 0xe85d75, 0x38b2ac, 0xf6a623, 0x48bb78, 0xed64a6\];

const CHAR_COLORS = ALL_CHAR_COLORS.slice(0, N);

\`\`\`

\`\`\`

\`\`\`

\> NOTE: The existing \`const charSprites\`, \`const charTex\`, \`const charOrigH\` declarations

\> that come later in the file must be **\*\*removed\*\*** to avoid duplicate declarations. Find and

\> delete:

\> \`\`\`

**\### Step 4C --- Fix \`TOTAL\` to use real feature count**

\`\`\`js

const TOTAL = 2 + DEMO.features.length;

**\### Step 4D --- Fix narrator intro text to reflect real candidate/feature count**

  }

async function init() {

  document.getElementById(\'next-btn\').disabled=true;

  document.getElementById(\'next-btn\').textContent=\'Loading sprites\...\';

  // Update page title to reflect actual decision context

  const isRealData = DEMO !== DEMO_FALLBACK;

  if (isRealData) {

    document.title = \`Decision Visualizer --- \${DEMO.winner} vs \${DEMO.candidates.filter(c =\> c !== DEMO.winner).join(\' vs \')}\`;

    setNarrator(\`Real decision loaded: \${DEMO.candidates.length} candidates, \${DEMO.features.length} criteria. Press Begin when ready.\`, \'neutral\');

  }

  drawBG(); drawPlatforms();

  await loadTextures();

  spawnChars();

  updateProgress(0, TOTAL);

  if (!isRealData) {

    setNarrator(\'All candidates present. Press Begin when ready.\', \'neutral\');

  }

  document.getElementById(\'next-btn\').disabled=false;

  document.getElementById(\'next-btn\').textContent=\'Begin →\';

  hideIdealBadge();

}

Antigravity Sonnet tried to fix it : Root Cause Analysis There were two bugs preventing real data from reaching the visualizer: Bug 1 --- Wrong storage API (

sessionStorage

→

localStorage

)

sessionStorage

is tab-scoped --- each new browser tab gets its own isolated session storage. When

window.open(\'/visualizer_prototype.html\', \'\_blank\')

opens a new tab, that tab has an empty sessionStorage and never sees the data stored by the parent tab.

Fix: Changed both script.js and visualizer_prototype.html to use

localStorage

, which is shared across all tabs of the same origin.

Bug 2 --- Null winner breaks validation The loadDemoData() validator checked

d.winner

as a truthy value. But

result.winner

is

null

when all candidates tie (epsilon \< 0.001). A tied result would silently fall back to the demo.

Fix: Changed

d.winner

→

\'winner\' in d

--- a structural check that passes for

null

values.

Verification

Validation PASSES: true

Tie case (winner=null) validation PASSES: true All 10 required fields (

candidates

,

features

,

weights

, raw,

normed

,

normedIdeals

,

detailed_breakdown

,

ranking

,

winner

,

explanation

) are confirmed present in the API response chain.

To test: Run

cd backend && npm run dev

, complete a decision, and click 🎬 Animate Result --- the visualizer console should now say

\[Visualizer\] Using real data for: \[your candidates\]

instead of the fallback message.

# Prompt 122 : Server.js checked

Yes, You may also Verify app.post(\"/api/calculate\", async (req, res) =\> {

try {

const { products_data, features, weights_raw, ideals, directions, metadata } =

req.body;

const result = calculateDecision(products_data, features, weights_raw, ideals, directions);

// Attach input source metadata so the frontend can show badges

if (metadata) {

for (const product of Object.keys(result.detailed_breakdown)) {

for (const feature of features) {

if (metadata\[product\]?.\[feature\]) {

result.detailed_breakdown\[product\]\[feature\].inputSource =

metadata\[product\]\[feature\].source;

result.detailed_breakdown\[product\]\[feature\].confidence =

metadata\[product\]\[feature\].confidence;

}

}

}

}

// Generate AI narrative explanation (Phase 1 --- unchanged)

const { explanation, source } = await generateExplanation(result, features, products_data);

const styles = build4Styles(result, features, products_data);

res.json({

\...result,

explanation,

explanation_source: source,

explanation_styles: styles,

raw: products_data,

});

} catch (error) {

console.error(\"Calculation error:\", error.message);

res.status(500).json({ error: error.message });

}

});

# Prompt 128 : Starting Phase 2

-   What was the issue I diagnosed The app was running a stale runtime context (cached/old frontend asset or wrong file copy), so the visualizer booted before valid injected payload was visible and kept falling back to demo. Your logs (fallback + loadInjectedData() called) indicated old parent behavior was still in play, not the intended current source path.

-   What solution I implemented I enforced a single runtime source-of-truth in served frontend files and added cache-busting/version markers so stale copies cannot win:

    1.  index.html: versioned script include (script.js?v=runtime-source-fix-2026-02-25-1).

    2.  script.js: parent window now stores **VISUALIZER_DATA** + **VISUALIZER_SOURCE** before iframe boot, and iframe loads with cache-busted URL (/visualizer_prototype.html?build=\...&ts=\...).

    3.  visualizer_prototype.html: logs build + parent source, reads injected parent data first, and logs explicit validation failure reason when injected payload is present but invalid.

-

3.  Character assignment was fixed-length, so scaling beyond existing slots wasn't truly generic, and char4/char5 were not wired into sprite loading. What was the solution implemented
